in Austria in the year 1983. My mother was a nurse and my father a Romanian immigrant who did almost every imaginable job for a while, from taxi driver to crane operator. From 1986 I was no longer allowed to play in the sandbox because of Chernobyl and my father's fear of all kinds of bacteria living in the dirt. In my early years, my best friend was TV and my first contact with the concept of digital image was a Commodore 64. In 1998, I attended a school for graphic design, which I finished successfully in 2003. Afterwards, I studied architecture in Graz in order to find out more about the possibilities of 3d animation and to extend my strategies for creating graphics and typography. In 2002, I started to make visuals for all kinds of electronic music. One of my hobbies is to collect strange examples of visual information on the internet, such as manuals of any kind, construction plans, fashion tablets and anatomic illustrations, and to combine them into new semantic chains and stories by means of video editing. Since 2005 I have been studying digital arts under Peter Weibel and Thomas F\xfcrstner at the University of Applied Arts in Vienna. My points of interest are varied but all leading to a simple goal: to tell my own tales, in my own style, and to manifest my personal notion of the world using every available tool. at the intersection between art, technology and finance. We conceive art as an exploration avenue to help us reflect and understand the social practices stemming from new technologies. Just as industrial production and mass media defined bureaucratic capitalism during the second half of the 20th C, we believe that the interactivity promoted by the computer revolution and new media are leading to new forms of social organization in contemporary times. We are interested in exploring those new organizational forms.\n\nIn the past three decades, the capital markets have been a leading adopter of digital interactivity. With the creation of electronic markets such as the Nasdaq in 1971 and Bloomberg terminals in 1981, Wall Street had its own Intranet two decades before other industries. Nowadays, electronic markets have replaced the traditional face-to-face exchanges in almost all of Europe. In this context, derivart examines social change at the beginning of the 21st C. by focussing on interactivity and new media in the capital markets.
